<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">New Zealand Football Championship</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p>The <b>New Zealand Football Championship</b> (NZFC, known as the <b>Stirling Sports Premiership</b> from 2016 for sponsorship reasons) is the national <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> league in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. It is a semi-professional/professional league that is operated by <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Football" title="New Zealand Football">New Zealand Football</a>. The league is run separately from various Winter regional club <a href="/wiki/Association_football_in_New_Zealand" title="Association football in New Zealand">competitions</a>, and many of the teams competing are <a href="/wiki/Professional_sports_league_organization" title="Professional sports league organization">franchises</a> jointly run by Winter clubs. It is currently <a href="/wiki/Sponsor_(commercial)" title="Sponsor (commercial)">sponsored</a> by Stirling Sports.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_format">Competition format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Competition format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are two stages to the competition; "<b>The League</b>" (commonly referred to as "regular season") and "<b>The Championship</b>" (commonly referred to as "the playoffs").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The two teams that win the league phase (the "Minor Premier") and the Grand Final (the "champion") qualify for the <a href="/wiki/OFC_Champions_League" title="OFC Champions League">OFC Champions League</a>. Should the same team win both the Minor Premiership and the Championship, the second Champions League spot is granted to the league runner-up. This has occurred on numerous occasions; the first instance being in 2006 when Auckland City (premiers and champions) and Young Heart Manawatu qualified despite Canterbury United contesting the Grand Final.</p>
<p>There are no lower divisions in the Premiership, thus no <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">promotion and relegation</a> exists, similar to leagues in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_League">The League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For the first four seasons, regular season had the teams play each other three times, however, this was changed to the present 14-match system in 2008, due to financial difficulties affecting some of the clubs. At the end of the regular season, the top four teams progress to the playoffs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Championship">The Championship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Championship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The playoffs are run as a home-and-away semi-finals series, with the winners progressing to a one-match Grand Final.</p>
<p>The playoff phase in the inaugural season was contested by the top three clubs, whereby the Minor Premier (winner of league phase) received a bye and hosting rights for the grand final, with second and third placed teams playing off in a one-game preliminary final. The NZFC experimented with a five team playoff in the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_New_Zealand_Football_Championship" title="2005–06 New Zealand Football Championship">2005–06 season</a>, however, this was discontinued and the league reverted to the three-team playoff system for the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_New_Zealand_Football_Championship" title="2006–07 New Zealand Football Championship">2006–07</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_New_Zealand_Football_Championship" title="2007–08 New Zealand Football Championship">2007–08</a> seasons.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_in_2004_to_present">Establishment in 2004 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Establishment in 2004 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The New Zealand Football Championship was created as a replacement to the former <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_National_Soccer_League" title="New Zealand National Soccer League">New Zealand National Soccer League</a>, a tournament involving clubs from the regional governing bodies of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Football" title="New Zealand Football">New Zealand Football</a>. The NZFC was to be run as a summer league involving new clubs created solely for the new competition, with these new clubs being run jointly by existing winter clubs. The only exception to this was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napier_City_Rovers" title="Napier City Rovers">Napier City Rovers</a>, whose summer club would be rebranded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawke%27s_Bay_United" title="Hawke's Bay United">Hawke's Bay United</a> during the second season, to be operated jointly by other clubs in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawke%27s_Bay" title="Hawke's Bay">Hawke's Bay</a> region.</p>
<p>Eleven groups bid for franchises, with the successful bids being announced on 7 April 2004 as <a href="/wiki/Auckland_City_FC" title="Auckland City FC">Auckland City</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canterbury_United" title="Canterbury United">Canterbury United</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawke%27s_Bay_United" title="Hawke's Bay United">Napier City Rovers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otago_United" title="Otago United">Otago United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_Wellington" title="Team Wellington">Team Wellington</a>, <a href="/wiki/WaiBOP_United" title="WaiBOP United">Waikato FC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waitakere_United" title="Waitakere United">Waitakere United</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/YoungHeart_Manawatu" title="YoungHeart Manawatu">YoungHeart Manawatu</a>, with Olé Madrids, East Auckland and Team Bay of Plenty being excluded. Unhappy at their exclusion, the Olé Madrids bid team took New Zealand Soccer to court, suing for damages and demanding inclusion in the competition, claiming that, whilst they met NZ Soccer's criteria for inclusion, other successful bids did not. The case was dropped by the Madrids team eight days before the commencement of the first NZFC season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Western Suburbs, the club associated with the Olé Academy, is now a principal member of the Team Wellington franchise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ole_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ole-3">[3]</a></sup> East Auckland also considered legal action, however this was not pursued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Franchises_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Franchises-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first match of the competition was on 15 October 2004, with <a href="/wiki/Auckland_City_FC" title="Auckland City FC">Auckland City</a> defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawke%27s_Bay_United" title="Hawke's Bay United">Napier City Rovers</a> 3–1 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bluewater_Stadium" title="Bluewater Stadium">Park Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napier,_New_Zealand" title="Napier, New Zealand">Napier</a>. Auckland City were also crowned the inaugural NZFC champions after defeating <a href="/wiki/Waitakere_United" title="Waitakere United">Waitakere United</a> 3–2 in the final.</p>
<p>The second season saw Napier City Rovers rebrand and re-organize their NZFC team as Hawke's Bay United, forming an amalgamated franchise with other local clubs. It also saw the first instance of a NZFC team winning the <a href="/wiki/OFC_Champions_League" title="OFC Champions League">O-League</a>, with Auckland City FC defeating <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesian</a> team <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AS_Pirae" title="AS Pirae">AS Pirae</a> 3–1.</p>
<p>At the conclusion of the 2006–07 season, New Zealand Football granted three-season licence extensions to seven of the eight franchises – all but <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/YoungHeart_Manawatu" title="YoungHeart Manawatu">YoungHeart Manawatu</a>, who had to re-apply due to concerns over the club's financial and organisational situation. However, YoungHeart eventually earned reinstatement after beating out four rival bids – one based in <a href="/wiki/Gisborne,_New_Zealand" title="Gisborne, New Zealand">Gisborne</a>, one from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Shore_City" title="North Shore City">North Shore City</a>, and two from <a href="/wiki/Manukau_City" title="Manukau City">Manukau</a>. Olé Madrids also applied for the licence, however they withdrew early.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Licence_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Licence-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 September 2010, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Football" title="New Zealand Football">New Zealand Football</a> announced a five-year sponsorship agreement with <a href="/wiki/ASB_Bank" title="ASB Bank">ASB Bank</a> resulting in the rebranding of the New Zealand Football Championship to the ASB Premiership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASB_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-ASB-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, after a review of the competition by the ASB Premiership review committee, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/YoungHeart_Manawatu" title="YoungHeart Manawatu">YoungHeart Manawatu</a> was dropped from the competition after finishing last in the previous three seasons. New Zealand Football also confirmed that a team composed of New Zealand players born on or after 1 January 1995 would take Manawatu's place in the Premiership for at least two seasons. The addition of the team – to be known as Wanderers SC – was to provide adequate preparation for New Zealand's U-20 players for the upcoming <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2015 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2015 FIFA U-20 World Cup</a> which will be hosted by New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wanderers_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wanderers-7">[7]</a></sup> Much confusion surrounded the initials "SC" in the Wanderers' name, as no official explanation was given as to what they stood for. It wasn't until after their first match that coach <a href="/wiki/Darren_Bazeley" title="Darren Bazeley">Darren Bazeley</a> finally revealed that "SC" stood for "Special Club", saying "it acknowledges this team has arisen out of a special situation and was specially formed for the purpose."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-_8-0"><a href="#cite_note--8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 2014–15 season saw the Premiership expand to nine teams for the first time in its history. <a href="/wiki/Wellington_Phoenix_FC_Reserves" title="Wellington Phoenix FC Reserves">Wellington Phoenix Reserves</a> was added to the competition to provide game time for the members of the Phoenix squad who are not playing frequently for the first team in the A-League. Restrictions were also put in place for all clubs requiring that at least 50% of match day squads are players who are eligible to play for the All Whites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Phoenix_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Phoenix-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>After 11 full seasons, only <a href="/wiki/Auckland_City_FC" title="Auckland City FC">Auckland City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waitakere_United" title="Waitakere United">Waitakere United</a> have been crowned Premiers or Champions, with Auckland City adding their sixth premiership and sixth title in the 2014–15 season. This trend was bucked, however, in the twelfth season of the competition, as Team Wellington defeated Auckland City 4-2 aet in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Expansion">2016 Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2016 Expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2015 it was announced that the league would be expanding to 10 teams for the 2016–17 season with <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Suburbs_AFC" title="Eastern Suburbs AFC">Eastern Suburbs</a> from Auckland, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamilton_Wanderers" title="Hamilton Wanderers">Hamilton Wanderers</a> from Hamilton, and <a href="/wiki/Tasman_United" title="Tasman United">Tasman United</a> from <a href="/wiki/Nelson,_New_Zealand" title="Nelson, New Zealand">Nelson</a> joining the league, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WaiBop_United" title="WaiBop United">WaiBop United</a> will exit the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2016 it was announced that the expanded league would be re-branded as the <b>Stirling Sports Premiership</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Clubs">Clubs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Clubs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are currently ten clubs from <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> playing in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_New_Zealand_Football_Championship" title="2016–17 New Zealand Football Championship">2016–17 Stirling Sports Premiership</a>. Unlike most European leagues, there is no system for <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">promotion and relegation</a>. This system is similar to leagues in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_changes">Name changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Name changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Napier_City_Rovers_FC" title="Napier City Rovers FC">Napier City Rovers</a> → <a href="/wiki/Hawke%27s_Bay_United_FC" title="Hawke's Bay United FC">Hawke's Bay United</a></b></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Southern_United_FC" title="Southern United FC">Otago United</a> → <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_FC" title="Southern United FC">Southern United</a></b></li>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waikato_FC" title="Waikato FC">Waikato FC</a> → <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waikato_FC" title="Waikato FC">WaiBOP United</a></b></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Champions_and_premiers">Champions and premiers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Champions and premiers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The teams that win the league phase (the "premier") and the Grand Final (the "champion") qualify for the <a href="/wiki/OFC_Champions_League" title="OFC Champions League">OFC Champions League</a>. Should the same team win both the Premiership and the Championship, the second O-League spot will be granted to league runner-up.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_of_the_Decade_Awards">Team of the Decade Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Team of the Decade Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, to celebrate the first 10 years of the league under the franchise format (2004-05 to 2013-14), New Zealand Football announced an official Team of the Decade and five individual player awards. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TotD_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-TotD-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PotD_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-PotD-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_of_the_Decade">Team of the Decade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Team of the Decade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Prior to the ASB Premiership Grand Final in 2014, the Team of the Decade was announced, as selected by a panel of media experts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PotD_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-PotD-21">[21]</a></sup> The team was selected in a 4-3-3 formation.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Players_of_the_Decade">Players of the Decade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Players of the Decade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Throughout the 2013-14 national league season, four Player of the Decade awards (based on playing position) were announced and prior to the 2014 Grand Final an overall Player of the Decade was announced. These awards were decided by a panel of media experts with input from fans via a public vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TotD_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-TotD-20">[20]</a></sup></p>

<th>Player</th>
<th>Club(s)</th>
</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_competitions">Related competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Related competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="OFC_Champions_League">OFC Champions League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: OFC Champions League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/OFC_Champions_League" title="OFC Champions League">OFC Champions League</a></div>
<p>The <b>OFC Champions League</b>, also known as the <b>O-League</b>, is the premier football competition in Oceania. It is organized by the OFC, Oceania's football governing body. It has been organized since 2007 under the current format, following its successor, the Oceania Club Championship. Two teams from the Stirling Sports Premiership participate annually. Four O-League titles have been won by teams from New Zealand.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ASB_Charity_Cup">ASB Charity Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: ASB Charity Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Charity_Cup" title="Charity Cup">Charity Cup</a></div>
<p>The <b>ASB Charity Cup</b> was introduced in 2011 as a season opener played the weekend before the first matches of the ASB Premiership season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-26">[26]</a></sup> The fixture pits the ASB Premiership Grand Final winner against the best performing New Zealand team in the OFC Champions League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-26">[26]</a></sup> However, when the same team fills both categories as Auckland City did in 2014 and 2015 the ASB Premiership runner-up qualifies for Charity Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ASB_Phoenix_Challenge">ASB Phoenix Challenge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: ASB Phoenix Challenge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=ASB_Phoenix_Challenge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="ASB Phoenix Challenge (page does not exist)">ASB Phoenix Challenge</a></div>
<p>The 2010–11 season saw the introduction of the ASB Challenge Series. This was an individual friendly competition in which the eight Premiership teams competed against a reserve team attached to <a href="/wiki/Wellington_Phoenix_FC" title="Wellington Phoenix FC">Wellington Phoenix FC</a>, a New Zealand-based team playing in the Australian <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a>. The ASB Phoenix Challenge was discontinued after the 2010–11 season but reinstated for 2012–2013.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Youth_League">National Youth League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: National Youth League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>New Zealand Football also runs the Under-20 <b>National Youth League</b>. The 2011/12 season consists of two four-team conferences (North and South) that play against each conference opponent twice (home and away), for six regular season games. At the conclusion of the youth league regular season, the top ranked Northern team hosts the second ranked Southern team, and the top ranked Southern team hosts the second ranked Northern team for the semi finals. The winners of these matches will face each other in the grand final. The current Youth League champion is Canterbury United, having defeated Waitakere United 2 – 1 after extra time at Bill McKinlay Park, <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> For the 2012–13 season the competition was expanded to 10 teams with the Nelson Falcons competing in the southern conference and Northern U17's connected to the New Zealand national team in the Northern conference.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="White_Ribbon_Cup">White Ribbon Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: White Ribbon Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/White_Ribbon_Cup" title="White Ribbon Cup">White Ribbon Cup</a></div>
<p><b>The White Ribbon Cup</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knockout</a> cup competition run by New Zealand Football. The 2011–12 season will be the inaugural season of the NZF Cup.</p>
<p>It was established in 2011 to provide regular football for the six clubs not participating in the Oceania Champions League and runs in conjunction with the Stirling Sports Premiership regular season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White_Ribbon_Cup_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-White_Ribbon_Cup-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;margin-left:1em;font-size:90%;">
<tr>
<th>Season</th>
<th>Winner</th>
<th>Score</th>
<th>Runner-up</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2011–12</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Team_Wellington" title="Team Wellington">Team Wellington</a></td>
<td>6–1</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waikato_FC" title="Waikato FC">Waikato FC</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Referees">Referees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Zealand_Football_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Referees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Referees are selected from around New Zealand and occasionally include guest referees from other nations, most notably Australia. Whilst the match referees may travel to games outside their home federation, assistant referees and fourth officials are from generally within the hosting federation.</p>
